## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of time and velocity. In nonlinear oscillator systems, the acceleration typically depends on position (which relates to velocity through integration) and velocity itself through restoring forces, damping, and nonlinear terms like cubic stiffness (Duffing) or nonlinear damping (van der Pol).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force (from velocity integral): dv_dt = c0 * v (simple proportional relationship)
- Linear damping + restoring: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * t (linear ODE approximation)
- Duffing-type cubic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (cubic restoring force in velocity space)
- Van der Pol damping: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v (nonlinear damping with amplitude-dependent sign)
- Polynomial nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 + c2 * v**3 (general polynomial restoring/damping)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * v**5 (higher-order nonlinear oscillator)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 (nonlinear damping variant)
- Trigonometric restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * v) (pendulum-like nonlinearity)
- Damped sinusoidal forcing: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (driven oscillator)
- Combined nonlinear + periodic: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (driven Duffing oscillator)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v * abs(v) (velocity-squared damping preserving sign)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v * cos(c1 * t) (time-varying stiffness)
- Negative stiffness + cubic: dv_dt = c0 * v - c1 * v**3 (double-well potential dynamics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Self-sustained oscillation (limit cycles) → Terms like (1 - v²)*v indicating amplitude-dependent damping sign change (van der Pol type)
- Odd-symmetry restoring forces → Only odd powers of v (v, v³, v⁵) indicating symmetric potential wells
- Hardening/softening spring → Cubic term v³ with sign determining whether stiffness increases or decreases with amplitude
- Autonomous vs non-autonomous → If t appears explicitly (e.g., sin(c*t)), the system is driven; if only v appears, it is autonomous
- Energy injection at small amplitude, dissipation at large → Negative linear damping combined with positive cubic damping: c0*v + c1*v³ with opposite signs
- Phase space structure → Acceleration as polynomial in velocity suggests the system can be written as a potential system or dissipative system depending on symmetry
- Periodic driving → Sinusoidal functions of time sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicate external forcing
- Conservative vs dissipative → Even powers of v in dv/dt indicate dissipative terms; odd powers indicate conservative restoring forces
